Ticket: PFT-772
Issue id: 173020
Module: Attendance
Summary: Future attendance report
Role: Safeguarding & Attendance Administrator
Source: Sheet1 - Row 555
Comment: This formula calculates maximum possible attendance %age across the academic year:

 =ROUNDUP((((Term 1/100*38)+(Term 2/100*34)+(Term 3/100*30)+(Term 4/100*17)+(13)+(23)+(35))/190*100),1)

 It can be varied to show a particular Term (4):

 =ROUNDUP((((/100*38)+(/100*34)+(/100*30)+(/100*17)+(13))/132*100),1)

 The days passed and remaining days of the current term have to manually adjusted on the day the report runs to make it accurate. It would be great to have an Arbor report which adjusts the variables automatically on the day it runs.

Source: Sheet1 - Row 714
Comment: When uploading documents Arbor will only match to a student if the filename before the extension solely contains the unique identifier selected.

 This can cause practical issues. For example, when a student, parent, or staff member downloads a report to view it - they only identifying information is that unique identifier. Where multiple reports are downloaded, whether close together or over time, they will have a list of documents such as 2141.pdf, 2141(1).pdf, 2141(2).pdf - with no way of identifying what these documents relate to.

 How this is done - I would suggest a second check, should the initial "whole filename" check fail, which would search for brackets and check the string between them. This would still allow schools to continue to use just the id as filename if they chose to, while allowing you to parse the student ID easily from surrounding text and making the documents far more friendly once downloaded for a wide range of end users for schools that choose to describe documents in the filename. Brackets are not generally be used in the filenames except for duplicates (perhaps square brackets could be used to make sure there is even less issue of conflict)

Ticket: PFT-584
Issue id: 172566
Module: Assessments
Summary: Functionality of Target Setting Dashboards
Role: Data Lead
Source: Sheet1 - Row 743
Comment: I'm not 100% sure about this, but currently my understanding is that your school and MAT level dashboards indicate what proportion of children are working below, meeting or exceeding their year targets. Whilst this provides you with a universal performance measure it does not really meet the needs of heads/leaders at a school or MAT level.

 The key measures at a primary level are:

 KS2 Yr 6 proportion of pupils attaining the Expected Standard in reading, writing, maths and the combined reading, writing and maths measure.

 These are the measures that schools and MATs are held to account on by Ofsted and the RSC.

 A much better version of the dashboards would therefore be to have 4 dashboards to show the % of pupils targeted to attain the Expected Standard in each measure and the % of pupils currently on track to attain the each measure.

 This would be really good if it could be for all year groups and filterable down to one. And even better if it also had additional dashboards for GPS, EYFS Yr R GLD and KS1 Yr 1 Phonics, and also the last published national averages as benchmarks.

 This would transform the usefulness of your headline dashboard page which does not currently meet the needs of our heads or leaders in terms of pupils' in school attainment data.

Ticket: PFT-566
Issue id: 172523
Module: Meals
Summary: Meal Menus
Role: Administrator
Source: Sheet1 - Row 761
Comment: Was hoping to use Arbor to administer our meal choices, however it won't work for us currently.

 Let me explain what we currently do. We have a 3 week rotating menu (4 main choice and 3 desserts each day). I put it onto Google Forms and parents make their child's choices for all 3 weeks for both main choice and dessert. I collate the choices and give numbers to cook ahead of the menu starting. Any changes after we've collated numbers for the kitchen are made manually.

 I've spoken with our support team and I can't make Arbor work for the following reasons:

 1. There is no way for parents to choose puddings, just main courses. There is no workaround either that we can think of.

 2. Half-terms are included in the meal rotation which means that you have to do two meal menus for one term if you are running the menu for the whole of the term, otherwise the last week of half term may be week 1, and then half-term becomes week 2 which is not correct. This is extra time for me.

 3. Because of 2 above, parents will have to duplicate choices - choosing for 6 weeks instead of 3 weeks. This is extra time for them.

 4. Parents changing menu choices - I'm told that school do not get notified of menu choices and it only becomes apparent on the day of the meal that has been changed. This is too late as cook needs to order food in advance. I would like to be able to stop parents making changes once I've submitted the numbers to the kitchen so that they can be manually adjusted so cook knows what to order as we don't like surprises!

 I have decided to abandon using Arbor for our meal choices for the time being due to the above and we will continue using our existing system.

 If you do end up developing this side of Arbor, I would expect to see some reports which I could give to the kitchen so that they can see how many meals of each choice they need for each day for ordering purposes. I would also be keen to see one which has headers for each meal choice and the names of children underneath who have chosen this, sortable by class. This report is useful in the dining hall for MSAs to shout children's names out to come up and get their meal.

 Many thanks for reading!
